Polansky">\n          Polansky\n         </a>\n         <div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">\n          <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_program" title="Space Shuttle program">\n           Space Shuttle program\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <div style="width:100%">\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: left; text-align:left;padding-right:0.5em;">\n           \xe2\x86\x90\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n            STS-115\n           </a>\n          </div>\n          <div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;">\n           <a href="/wiki/STS-117" title="STS-117">\n            STS-117\n           </a>\n           \xe2\x86\x92\n          </div>\n         </div>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <p>\n       <b>\n        STS-116\n       </b>\n       was a\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle" title="Space Shuttle">\n        Space Shuttle\n       </a>\n       mission to the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       (ISS) flown by\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Discovery" title="Space Shuttle Discovery">\n        Space Shuttle\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </a>\n       .\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       lifted off on 9 December 2006 at 20:47:35\n       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Time_Zone" title="Eastern Time Zone">\n        EST\n       </a>\n       . A previous launch attempt on 7 December had been canceled due to cloud cover. It was the first night launch of a space shuttle since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-113" title="STS-113">\n        STS-113\n       </a>\n       in November 2002.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The mission is also referred to as\n       <b>\n        ISS-12A.1\n       </b>\n       by the ISS program. The main goals of the mission were delivery and attachment of the International Space Station\'s\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        P5 truss\n       </a>\n       segment, a major rewiring of the station\'s power system, and exchange of ISS\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_14" title="Expedition 14">\n        Expedition 14\n       </a>\n       personnel. The shuttle landed at 17:32 EST on 22 December 2006 at\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center" title="Kennedy Space Center">\n        Kennedy Space Center\n       </a>\n       98 minutes off schedule due to unfavorable weather conditions. This mission was particularly notable to Sweden, being the first spaceflight of a Scandinavian astronaut (\n       <a href="/wiki/Christer_Fuglesang" title="Christer Fuglesang">\n        Christer Fuglesang\n       </a>\n       ).\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       STS-116 was the final scheduled space shuttle launch from\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Pad 39B\n       </a>\n       as\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       reconfigured it for\n       <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n        Ares I\n       </a>\n       launches.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pad39b_5-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-pad39b-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The only remaining use of Pad 39B by the shuttle was as a reserve for the\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-400" title="STS-400">\n        STS-400\n       </a>\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Launch_On_Need" title="Launch On Need">\n        Launch On Need\n       </a>\n       mission to rescue the crew of\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-125" title="STS-125">\n        STS-125\n       </a>\n       , the final\n       <a href="/wiki/Hubble_Space_Telescope" title="Hubble Space Telescope">\n        Hubble Space Telescope\n       </a>\n       servicing mission, if their shuttle became damaged.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After STS-116,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       entered a period of maintenance. Its next mission would be\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-120" title="STS-120">\n        STS-120\n       </a>\n       starting on 23 October 2007.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <div class="toc" id="toc">\n       <div class="toctitle">\n        <h2>\n         Contents\n        </h2>\n       </div>\n       <ul>\n        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1">\n         <a href="#Crew">\n </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       Originally this mission was to carry the\n       <a Wilcutt">\n          Terry Wilcutt\n         </a>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th scope="row">\n         Pilot\n        </th>\n        <td colspan="2">\n         <span class="flagicon">\n          <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">\n           <img alt="United States" class="thumbborder" data-file-height="650" data-file-width="1235" height="12" Kaleri\n         </a>\n         ,\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_Federal_Space_Agency" title="Russian Federal Space Agency">\n          RKA\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         <a href="/wiki/Expedition_7" title="Expedition 7">\n          Expedition 7\n         </a>\n         <br/>\n         ISS Flight Engineer\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_highlights">\n        Mission highlights\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mission highlights">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1952" data-file-width="2816" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg/220px-ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg/330px-ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/06/ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg/440px-ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:ISS_after_STS-116_in_December_2006.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         A photograph of the\n         <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n          ISS\n         </a>\n         after STS-116 with the new\n         <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n          P5 truss segment\n         </a>\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        The STS-116 mission\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISS_assembly_sequence" title="ISS assembly sequence">\n         delivered and attached\n        </a>\n        the\n        <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n         International Space Station\n        </a>\n        \'s third port truss segment, the\n        <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n         P5 truss\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The STS-116 mission brought to the Station\n        <a href="/wiki/Expedition_14" title="Expedition 14">\n         Expedition 14\n        </a>\n        crew member\n        <a href="/wiki/Sunita_Williams" title="Sunita Williams">\n         Sunita Williams\n        </a>\n        (who subsequently established a record for most time in space for a female astronaut) and brought home Expedition 14 crew member\n        <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Reiter" title="Thomas Reiter">\n         Thomas Reiter\n        </a>\n        from European Space Agency (launched by\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-121" title="STS-121">\n         STS-121\n        </a>\n        ).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Christer_Fuglesang" title="Christer Fuglesang">\n         Christer Fuglesang\n        </a>\n        became Sweden\'s first astronaut. His flight was a rare occurrence of two\n        <a href="/wiki/European_Astronaut_Corps" title="European Astronaut Corps">\n         ESA astronauts\n        </a>\n        flying in space together.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The third of three\n        <a href="/wiki/SPHERES" title="SPHERES">\n         SPHERES\n        </a>\n        testbeds launched to the ISS.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Astronauts completed major rewiring of the\n        <a href="/wiki/Electrical_system_of_the_International_Space_Station" title="Electrical system of the International Space Station">\n         electrical system of the International Space Station\n        </a>\n        in order to bring online the P3/P4\n        <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure#Solar_arrays" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n         solar array\n        </a>\n        installed by\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-115" title="STS-115">\n         STS-115\n        </a>\n        in September 2006.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Additional rewiring was done to ISS Pressurized Mating Adapter 2 (PMA2) to enable\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Electrical_system_of_the_International_Space_Station" title="Electrical system of the International Space Station">\n          Station-Shuttle Power Transfer System\n         </a>\n         (SSPTS)\n        </i>\n        commencing with\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n         STS-118\n        </a>\n        .\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n         <a href="#cite_note-7">\n          [7]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">\n         <a href="#cite_note-8">\n          [8]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aiaa_SSPTS_9-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-aiaa_SSPTS-9">\n          [9]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-apcu_mass_10-0">\n         <a href="#cite_note-apcu_mass-10">\n          [10]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        One half of the original P6 solar array installed by\n        <a href="/wiki/STS-97" title="STS-97">\n         STS-97\n        </a>\n        was folded to make room for the new P4 array deployed by STS-115 to rotate and track the sun.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        STS-116 was the last STS mission scheduled for launch from pad 39B. The pad will be refitted for upcoming\n        <a href="/wiki/Ares_I" title="Ares I">\n         Ares I\n        </a>\n        launches.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pad39b_5-1">\n         <a href="#cite_note-pad39b-5">\n          [5]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        The crew of STS-116 consisted of five rookie astronauts. Only Mission Commander\n        <a href="/wiki/Mark_L._Polansky" title="Mark L. Polansky">\n         Mark Polansky\n        </a>\n        (2) and Mission specialist\n        <a href="/wiki/Robert_Curbeam" title="Robert Curbeam">\n         Robert Curbeam\n        </a>\n        (3) had previously flown in space.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Robert Curbeam became the first astronaut to make four\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extra-vehicular_activity" title="Extra-vehicular activity">\n         EVAs\n        </a>\n        during the same mission.\n        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n         <a href="#cite_note-11">\n          [11]\n         </a>\n        </sup>\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        This was the first mission with two African-American crewmembers.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_notes">\n        Mission notes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Mission notes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       As one of the main goals of STS-116 was to exchange\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        ISS\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Expedition_14" title="Expedition 14">\n        Expedition 14\n       </a>\n       crew members, the crew of STS-116 changed mid-flight. ISS Flight Engineer\n       <a href="/wiki/Sunita_Williams" title="Sunita Williams">\n        Sunita "Suni" Williams\n       </a>\n       was part of the STS-116 crew for the first portion of the mission. She then replaced ISS Flight Engineer\n       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Reiter" title="Thomas Reiter">\n        Thomas Reiter\n       </a>\n       on the Expedition 14 crew and Reiter joined the STS-116 crew for the return to Earth.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Final_Assembly_Power_Converter_Unit_mission_for_Discovery">\n        Final Assembly Power Converter Unit mission for\n        <i>\n         Discovery\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Final Assembly Power Converter Unit mission for Discovery">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       During planned orbiter upgrades that took place subsequent to this mission,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\'\n       </i>\n       s\n       <i>\n        Assembly Power Converter Units\n       </i>\n       (APCUs) were removed and replaced with the shuttle-side components of the Station-Shuttle Power Transfer System (SSPTS). The APCUs converted 28VDC orbiter main bus power to 124VDC, compatible with the ISS\'s 120VDC main bus power. During initial station assembly missions, orbiter APCU power was used to augment the power available from the Russian service segment. With the operation of permanent main electrical systems (e.g. P4 array and SARJ, MBSUs, DDCUs, Ammonia cooling systems), orbiter power was no longer needed by the ISS.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       After\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-118" title="STS-118">\n        STS-118\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       drew power from the ISS, although\n       <i>\n        Atlantis\n       </i>\n       was never upgraded with the SSPTS. This system slowed the orbiters\' consumption of hydrogen and oxygen used by their onboard electricity-generating fuel cells. The hydrogen and oxygen supplies, stored cryogenically in tanks aboard the orbiter, limited the duration of Space Shuttle missions. As a result of the changeover to SSPTS,\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        Endeavour\n       </i>\n       gained approximately 50% of the time that would have been spent docked otherwise. This resulted in 2\xe2\x80\x934 extra days for each ISS-docked mission.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shuttle_payloads_apcu_12-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shuttle_payloads_apcu-12">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mei_spdu_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-mei_spdu-13">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts-98-eva-ref_15-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts-98-eva-ref-15">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sts116_ascent_16-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-sts116_ascent-16">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shuttle_payloads_spdu_17-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-shuttle_payloads_spdu-17">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_payloads">\n        Mission payloads\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Mission payloads">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:P5_Truss_segment_prepared_for_launch_on_STS-116.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/P5_Truss_segment_prepared_for_launch_on_STS-116.jpg/330px-P5_Truss_segment_prepared_for_launch_on_STS-116.jpg 1.5x,   <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:P5_Truss_segment_prepared_for_launch_on_STS-116.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         In the Space Station Processing Facility, an overhead crane moves the P5 truss for mission STS-116 to the payload canister.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n       <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:09_ICC_STS-116.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         ICC STS-116\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <div    <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Discovery_Payload_Bay_STS-116.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Discovery\'s\n         </i>\n         payload bay, containing the\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SPACEHAB" title="SPACEHAB">\n          SPACEHAB\n         </a>\n         module and ISS P5 Truss.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The primary payload for the STS-116 mission was the\n       <a href="/wiki/Integrated_Truss_Structure" title="Integrated Truss Structure">\n        P5 Truss\n       </a>\n       segment of the\n       <a href="/wiki/International_Space_Station" title="International Space Station">\n        International Space Station\n       </a>\n       . The shuttle also carried a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spacehab" title="Spacehab">\n        Spacehab\n       </a>\n       Logistics Module to resupply the ISS, and an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Integrated_Cargo_Carrier" title="Integrated Cargo Carrier">\n        Integrated Cargo Carrier\n       </a>\n       with four sub-satellites, which were deployed after undocking from the ISS: the\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_Neutral_Density_Experiment" title="Atmospheric Neutral Density Experiment">\n        ANDE\n       </a>\n       technology demonstrator (OSCAR 61 and 62), developed by the Naval Research Laboratory, and three\n       <a href="/wiki/CubeSat" title="CubeSat">\n        CubeSats\n       </a>\n       (\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=RAFT-1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="RAFT-1 (page does not exist)">\n        RAFT-1\n       </a>\n       (OSCAR 60) and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MARScom&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MARScom (page does not exist)">\n        MARScom\n       </a>\n       for the\n       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Naval_Academy" title="United States Naval Academy">\n        United States Naval Academy\n       </a>\n       , and\n       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=MEPSI_2A/2B&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="MEPSI 2A/2B (page does not exist)">\n        MEPSI 2A/2B\n       </a>\n       for\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Defense_Advanced_Research_Projects_Agency" title="Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency">\n        DARPA\n       </a>\n       ). It was the first Shuttle mission to deploy satellites since\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-113" title="STS-113">\n        STS-113\n       </a>\n       in 2002.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Location\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Cargo\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Mass\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 3\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Tunnel Adapter\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         112 kilograms (247\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n      <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-shuttle_payloads_spdu_17-1">\n           <a href="#cite_note-shuttle_payloads_spdu-17">\n            [17]\n           </a>\n          </sup>\n         </p>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         2 x 35 kilograms (77\xc2\xa0lb)\n         <p>\n          20 kilograms (44\xc2\xa0lb)\n         </p>\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Bay 7\xe2\x80\x938\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         Truss segment P5\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         1,860 kilograms (4,100\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr valign="top">\n        <td>\n         Bay 11\xe2\x80\x9312\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <table>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            Integrated Cargo Carrier\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            839 kilograms (1,850\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            STP-H2, FRAM\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            1,398 kilograms (3,082\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            Service Module Debris Panels\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            100 kilograms (220\xc2\xa0lb)?\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            RAFT-1\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            4 kilograms (8.8\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            MARScom\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            3 kilograms (6.6\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n    ANDE launch cylinder\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            20 kilograms (44\xc2\xa0lb)?\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            ANDE-MAA\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            50 kilograms (110\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n          <tr>\n           <td>\n            ANDE-FCAL\n           </td>\n           <td>\n            75 kilograms (165\xc2\xa0lb)\n           </td>\n          </tr>\n         </table>\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         total 2,942 kilograms (6,486\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Sill\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         OBSS (Orbital Boom Sensor System) 202\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         450 kilograms (990\xc2\xa0lb)?\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         Sill\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         RMS 303\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         390 kilograms (860\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </td>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Total 12,500 kilograms (27,600\xc2\xa0lb)\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n      </table>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_background">\n        Mission background\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mission background">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Rollout_(KSC-06PD-2474).jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg/220px-STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg/330px-STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/13/STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg/440px-STS-116_Rollout_%28KSC-06PD-2474%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Rollout_(KSC-06PD-2474).jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          Discovery\n         </i>\n         on its way to Launchpad 39B during rollout.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       STS-116 was planned (post\n       <a href="/wiki/STS-114" title="STS-114">\n        return-to-flight\n       </a>\n       ) to launch on 14 December 2006. But on 29 November 2006\n       <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">\n        NASA\n       </a>\n       announced that the launch team had been asked to aim for a launch on 7 December 2006 rather than the original target date of 14 December. The launch window for the STS-116 mission opened on 7 December and extended through 17 December. The seven-member flight crew arrived for launch at Kennedy\'s Shuttle Landing Facility on 3 December 2006 in the afternoon.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Primary payloads on the 13-day mission were the P5 integrated truss segment, SPACEHAB single logistics module, and an integrated cargo carrier. The STS-116 mission was the 20th Shuttle flight to the station.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Launch on the new, earlier date required a night-time launch. Subsequent to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Columbia_disaster" title="Space Shuttle Columbia disaster">\n        <i>\n         Columbia\n        </i>\n        disaster\n       </a>\n       , NASA had imposed rules requiring shuttle launches to be conducted during the day, when light would be sufficient for cameras to observe falling debris. With the redesign of shuttle tank foam having minimized the amount of falling debris and the availability of in-orbit inspection procedures, the daylight-launch requirement was relaxed.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Rollover of\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       to the\n       <a href="/wiki/Vehicle_Assembly_Building" title="Vehicle Assembly Building">\n        Vehicle Assembly Building\n       </a>\n       (VAB) occurred on 31 October, and on 1 November the orbiter was raised into a vertical orientation and moved into High Bay 3 to be mated with the\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_external_tank" title="Space Shuttle external tank">\n        external tank\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Space_Shuttle_Solid_Rocket_Booster" title="Space Shuttle Solid Rocket Booster">\n        solid rocket boosters\n       </a>\n       . Rollout to\n       <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n        Launch Complex 39B\n       </a>\n       was completed on Thursday 11 November.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The crew for the mission arrived at Kennedy Space Center on 13 November to begin their final four-day prelaunch training for the mission, which included familiarization activities, rehearsal of emergency procedures and practice on NASA\'s Shuttle Training Aircraft, along with a simulated countdown, which took place on the morning of 16 November 2006. The astronauts then traveled to\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lyndon_B._Johnson_Space_Center" title="Lyndon B. Johnson Space Center">\n        Johnson Space Center\n       </a>\n       in Houston, Texas, and returned to Kennedy Space Center on 3 December 2006, four days before the planned launch date.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The payloads for the mission, including a SPACEHAB module and the P5 truss, were loaded from the payload canister into\n       <i>\n        Discovery\'s\n       </i>\n       payload bay on 16 November, and, with the sealing of the payload bay doors, all that remained was to fill the external fuel tank before the\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       shuttle stack was in full launch configuration. With the completion of the Flight Readiness Review over 28\xe2\x80\x9329 November (which evaluated all activities and elements necessary for the safe and successful performance of the shuttle during the mission, including the Orbiter itself, the payload and flight crew),\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       was given her Certificate of Flight Readiness, the launch date was officially set to 7 December 2006, and the mission officially given the "Go" for launch.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_timeline">\n        Mission timeline\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Mission timeline">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <h3>\n       <span id="7_December_(Launch_attempt_1)">\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="7_December_.28Launch_attempt_1.29">\n        7 December (Launch attempt 1)\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=STS-116&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 7 December (Launch attempt 1)">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Boarding_(NASA_STS116-S-006)_2006-Dec-09.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2008" data-file-width="3000" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg/220px-STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg/330px-STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg/440px-STS-116_Boarding_%28NASA_STS116-S-006%29_2006-Dec-09.jpg 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:STS-116_Boarding_(NASA_STS116-S-006)_2006-Dec-09.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         STS-116 crew about to board the astrovan for the trip to pad\n         <a href="/wiki/Kennedy_Space_Center_Launch_Complex_39" title="Kennedy Space Center Launch Complex 39">\n          39B\n         </a>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Following the completion of the pre-launch preparations, all eyes were on the Florida skies, due to a forecast low cloud ceiling for the night of the launch. The mission\'s seven astronauts were loaded into\n       <i>\n        Discovery\n       </i>\n       ready for the scheduled launch at 21:37 EST, with hopes high for a break in the clouds, but as the scheduled launch time approached it became apparent that the cloud would not break, and the launch attempt was scrubbed, with the next attempt scheduled for 9 December 2006.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       Prior to the initial attempt on 7 December, NASA had determined that they would not attempt a launch on Friday because of a\n       <a href="/wiki/Surface_weather_analysis" title="Surface weather analysis">\n        cold front\n       </a>\n       moving in that eventually scrubbed Thursday\'s launch attempt.\n      </p>\n      <table class="wikitable">\n       <tr>\n        <th>\n         Attempt\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Planned\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Result\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Turnaround\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Reason\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Decision point\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Weather go (%)\n        </th>\n        <th>\n         Notes\n        </th>\n       </tr>\n       <tr>\n        <td>\n         1\n        </td>\n        <td>\n         <span
